  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_edf6006d-7f25-463e-ad8d-65ee95f2fff4'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<div id="review_490166721" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/490166721" />
    <a title="Christopher Godsoe" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5968115-christopher-godsoe"><img alt="Christopher Godsoe" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442601653p2/5968115.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/490166721?book_show_action=true">Dec 30, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christopher Godsoe" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christopher Godsoe" href="/user/show/5968115-christopher-godsoe">Christopher Godsoe</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer490166721" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2367104951668363277">This is an amazing series. I'd love to go into more detail, but why use 100 words when 5 will do? The characters are so well fleshed out, that when the time comes to say goodbye to them you will feel as though you are saying goodbye to friends. After reading the first book in this series, I devoured the remaining three over a week and a half (Audiobook versions). <br/><br/>There are parts that become repetitive, and my only complaint is that none of the main characters (except for Link) seem to be able to</span>
  <span id="freeText2367104951668363277" style="display:none">This is an amazing series. I'd love to go into more detail, but why use 100 words when 5 will do? The characters are so well fleshed out, that when the time comes to say goodbye to them you will feel as though you are saying goodbye to friends. After reading the first book in this series, I devoured the remaining three over a week and a half (Audiobook versions). <br /><br />There are parts that become repetitive, and my only complaint is that none of the main characters (except for Link) seem to be able to tell anyone else what is on their mind. In a world full of Incubus, Casters, Seers, and Keepers, it's really difficult at times to believe the lengths some of the characters will push their belief that no one around them understands what they are going through, or that they will believe what they say. <br /><br />The Audiobook versions are fantastic, Kevin T. Collins does such a great job with these characters. He conveys Amma's emotion, Links humor, and Macon's charm equally well, well enough that I worry that the forthcoming film adaptation might come up short, even with the amazing cast that they have lined up. <br /><br />In the end, with the conclusion of the series, the thing I am most looking forward to is the films, not because I think they will stick so close to the story (So much of this story takes place inside of the characters heads, it would be impossible), but because I will get to see all of my friends again. Knowing the faces of the actors cast for the films has allowed me to combine the excellent narration by Mr. Collins with a face, making the experience much more enjoyable.<br /><br />This series is nothing like what I normally read, but I'm glad I gave it a shot. The highest praise I can give it is that I am recommending it to all of my friends that read, and I know they will love it as much as I have.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2367104951668363277" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_599176397" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/599176397" />
    <a title="Samantha" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19725357-samantha"><img alt="Samantha" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1366784991p2/19725357.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/599176397?book_show_action=true">Apr 24, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

<div id="review_566166225" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/566166225" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/566166225?book_show_action=true">Mar 20, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amber" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amber" href="/user/show/7440008-amber">Amber</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7440008-amber?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7440008-amber?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7440008-amber?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7440008-amber?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7440008-amber?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer566166225" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8000955756062061290">This series started with the movie (which I was not a fan of). However, I kept thinking there has to be a good story somewhere and I'm so glad the movie lead me to these books. I couldn't put them down. I haven't found a series that drew me in like the Caster Chronicles in quite sometime. <br/><br/>Beautiful Creatures book #1 is about young Lena Duchannes who has moved in with her Uncle in Gatlin, South Carolina. Ethan Wates is a young man from Gatlin who has been dreaming of an unknown girl. When he meet</span>
  <span id="freeText8000955756062061290" style="display:none">This series started with the movie (which I was not a fan of). However, I kept thinking there has to be a good story somewhere and I'm so glad the movie lead me to these books. I couldn't put them down. I haven't found a series that drew me in like the Caster Chronicles in quite sometime. <br /><br />Beautiful Creatures book #1 is about young Lena Duchannes who has moved in with her Uncle in Gatlin, South Carolina. Ethan Wates is a young man from Gatlin who has been dreaming of an unknown girl. When he meets Lena he knows she is the girl who has been haunting his dreams. The two are pretty much instantly connected. <br /><br />Lena Duchannes is not your ordinary South Carolina girl. She comes from a family of castors. In their family on your 16th birthday your true light comes forth and you are claimed for either light or dark. <br /><br />The connection Lena and Ethan share, the mystery of the past, the visions there is so much I could share but I don't want to give any spoilers. It all leads up to one great book 1 in the Castor Chronicle Series .<br /><br />Book #2 Beautiful Darkness is even better than #1. Beautiful Darkness is very detailed, and the characters are both charming and complicated. You have the same characters from book 1 along with some new ones to mix it up a bit. Being from the South I absolutely love the Southern backdrop, lore and culture that is shared. You start out back in South Carolina and end up in Savannah Georgia one of my favorite places. <br /><br />Lena and Ethan are struggling with what happened on her 16th Birthday (book 1 you definitely want to read it first). Lena is almost paralyzed with the consequences of her actions. She can not face what she has done, or what is to come. Her grief and fear have her pushing Ethan away. After not being claimed by the dark in Beautiful Creatures you would have expected Lena to be happy. Instead this is where the story really is taking off. Lena's mother Saraphine is back and calling the seventeenth moon. Lena will still have to face the claiming and the ending will leave you shocked! <br /><br />This book shares a lot more of Amma, of Ethan's mother and the old kind of magic. I love the many different characters and how they are all working together or against each other for either light or dark to prevail. Secrets are coming out , mysteries being solved, and young love in the air .<br /><br />Book #3 Beautiful Chaos For me Beautiful Chaos began slower than the first two. It gets better and before its over I was doing the ugly cry as I read . This book is way darker than the first two. ONe thing for sure the characters you've grown to love are in for a lot of turmoil. <br /><br />Book #4 Goodbye Caster Chronicles. Book 4 is unlike the other three in this series. Where the first three books are all about Lena Duchane this book is all about Ethan Wate and his journey to return home. Beautiful Redemption is a solid ending to a very good YA series.<br /><br />"I guess that's the thing about a hero's journey. You might not start out a hero, and you might not even come back that way. But you change which is the same as everything changing. The journey changes whether or not you know it , whether or not you want it to. I had changed. "Ethan Wate.<br /><br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer2786112062767214646">I cannot even begin to explain my love for this series...<br/>It's been a long time since I've found a series of books that I literally fell in love with. This series is always on my mind so much to a point where I can't sleep for hours, that's probably not healthy. The characters are fabulous and the writing is beautiful. I'm actually completely in love with Ethan Wate he's perfect. Lena as much as she can be stupid in the second book is also very likable and relatable despite the fact the she is a </span>
  <span id="freeText2786112062767214646" style="display:none">I cannot even begin to explain my love for this series...<br />It's been a long time since I've found a series of books that I literally fell in love with. This series is always on my mind so much to a point where I can't sleep for hours, that's probably not healthy. The characters are fabulous and the writing is beautiful. I'm actually completely in love with Ethan Wate he's perfect. Lena as much as she can be stupid in the second book is also very likable and relatable despite the fact the she is a caster she's also just a teenage girl who wants to be accepted. The way that Ethan loves Lena and would do anything for her is absolutely adorable and I often find myself squealing while I'm reading these books. The romance is portrayed in such a way that makes it not cheesy and just perfect. Uncle Macon is frigging awesome, like seriously best uncle ever! My heart broke a little for Link each time Ridley rejected him. Of course Amma the epitome of the perfect mother figure, she loves Ethan with all of her heart and will not let anything lay a hand on him, she's sassy slightly terrifying but also very loving and strong. Liv of course I love she was such a great addition in the second book I love how her relationship grows with Lena. John Breed I love after reading the third one and I wished Ethan would just forgive him already. John and Liv's relationship is just so frigging adorable.<br />Each character in this series has a purpose in the long run, there are no random side characters that don't matter because that really bothers me when that happens!<br />The stories were captivating they got under your skin and stuck in your mind, I found myself physically not able to put the books down and go to sleep at night. These books are truly magnificent and I am so grateful that I came across them.<br />Kami Garcia and Margaret Stohl are geniuses. They are the best team ever! They're writing is just so beautiful and it works together so well!</span>

<div id="review_1021067254" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1021067254" />
    <a title="Anna Kis" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33789901-anna-kis"><img alt="Anna Kis" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1418709448p2/33789901.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1021067254?book_show_action=true">Aug 08, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anna Kis" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anna Kis" href="/user/show/33789901-anna-kis">Anna Kis</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">No one</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Anna by: </span>
      internet
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1021067254" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18084582391890513193">I personally did not enjoy this book series at all. I had to force myself to finish reading all four books; I had wanted to give up after the first few pages. <br/>The writing is incredibly bland, the characters 2d, and not only are you completely unable to relate to them, make a connection with them at any given time, you feel like punching them because of multiple reasons, one of them being their inability to express their feelings and explaining exactly what is going on with them. It would save so</span>
  <span id="freeText18084582391890513193" style="display:none">I personally did not enjoy this book series at all. I had to force myself to finish reading all four books; I had wanted to give up after the first few pages. <br />The writing is incredibly bland, the characters 2d, and not only are you completely unable to relate to them, make a connection with them at any given time, you feel like punching them because of multiple reasons, one of them being their inability to express their feelings and explaining exactly what is going on with them. It would save so much time if they could do just that.<br />All of the relationships have so much potential in the book, there are many couples you can root for, many different romantic story lines, but it is all ruined because of the poor writing. Instead of shipping the characters, you end up being annoyed by them - the couples that should be cute are just plain horrible, because of the forced romance the author forces on them. Instead of feelings gradually surfacing, instead of the characters staying true to themselves and their personalities as they fall in love, we have bland, dry romance that is not only incredibly sudden and uncalled for, with no background flirting, conversations, etc, but it is also so incredibly out of character, it hurts. <br />There were many times when I had to read a passage over and over again - and that is most definitely not because of my ability to read, but because it just made absolutely no sense. Events would happen so quickly, so much information would be dropped on you in one paragraph, but it would not be explained properly, and it ends up confusing you, and making the book less enjoyable.<br />Overall, the characters, the romance, even the slightly-cheesy and very-typical plot line has so much potential, but it is all ruined by the horrible writing.<br />I do not recommend the Beautiful Creatures series, I really do not. It is most definitely not worth your time.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="18084582391890513193" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_546472979" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/546472979" />
    <a title="Liz" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/714136-liz"><img alt="Liz" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1292253061p2/714136.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/546472979?book_show_action=true">Feb 25, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Liz" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Liz" href="/user/show/714136-liz">Liz</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer546472979&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer546472979" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14815095865108135817">Yeah, I admit it. I'm late to the party but I still read this series. The entire thing. On purpose.<br/><br/>I was looking for something light after reading something a bit more srs bsns than I'm used to, and the first book in the series was only about $7 on Kindle Fire, so I snagged it. (Call it research- I'm writing a teen supernatural romance.) The fact that the movie was supposed to come out about 2 weeks after I got the first book was a good impetus to speed through the whole series. And it was a sur</span>
  <span id="freeText14815095865108135817" style="display:none">Yeah, I admit it. I'm late to the party but I still read this series. The entire thing. On purpose.<br /><br />I was looking for something light after reading something a bit more srs bsns than I'm used to, and the first book in the series was only about $7 on Kindle Fire, so I snagged it. (Call it research- I'm writing a teen supernatural romance.) The fact that the movie was supposed to come out about 2 weeks after I got the first book was a good impetus to speed through the whole series. And it was a surprisingly enjoyable read.<br /><br />I'd give it a 5, but Garcia and Stohl really didn't get Ethan's voice quite right, imo. I know it's teen Goth, and I know that teen boys can be very soulful creatures, but Ethan knew a little to much about clothing, was a little too chaste, and a little too vague. Ethan says he wants to get out of Gatlin, but boyfriend doesn't really say where he'd rather go or what he'd do- which weakened his characterization considerably and makes him a bit of a lame duck protagonist. So in general, the Lena POV portions rang truer for me. I liked that they tried, though, and that the protagonist was a boy: Rather than have an odd girl move into town and fall in love with a local boy, they flipped the script and had the local boy woo the new girl in town. Who just happens to be supernatural and conflicted. Yeah, that.<br /><br />I liked that the character deaths were justified and made sense- Lena's mother, Abraham, and Hunting didn't need to be redeemed and the authors wisely didn't try. Sarafine got a bit of forgiveness at the end, but she still had to go. The ending was less saccharine than I expected- having the protagonist die and then come back from the Otherworld might have been cloying if it weren't worked out so well. That said, I'm not the target audience, so if I scoffed at the ease with which Ethan communicated his need for the river's eye to Lena and the way he got it from her from beyond the grave, where the Book of Moons retrieval turned out to be way more complicated, well, I'm a cynical old broad. I still liked it.<br /><br />Ridley, the evil cousin, played by Emmy Rossum in the movie, was hard to get a bead on. Her constant smack talk was tiresome- but again I'm older than the target audience, so for all I know she's a dream character for your average teen girl. Will have to ask a few teens what they thought.<br /><br />I enjoyed the world they built. The parameters were neatly explained, they treat their teen readers with respect- apparently they had a few teens go through and cut out "cheese" and generally act as betas, which served them well. There was one cheesy line and a few words that were just plain used wrong, and a bit of the denouement came right out of Halfblood Prince (and there's a reference to one of the characters' moms wanting to ban Harry Potter at the local library) but otherwise it's good.<br /><br />I'm sure I'll reread all four books and I can see myself passing my Kindle (or an actual paper copy) on to my girl cousins when they're old enough. Better this than Twilight, seriously.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14815095865108135817" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_729852820" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/729852820" />
    <a title="Camille" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/24288351-camille"><img alt="Camille" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1436196357p2/24288351.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/729852820?book_show_action=true">Sep 28, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Camille" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Camille" href="/user/show/24288351-camille">Camille</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer729852820" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10035457144179824206">So I realize I sorta missed the boat with this series as I believe the first one came out in like, 2009. But whatever. I am not really going to talk much about the plot, mostly because throughout 4 books of at least 500 pages each, THERE IS SO MUCH OF IT. However there might be Spoilers, But I’ll make sure and say so before.<br/><br/>I think the thing about these books is that they were pitted to be “the next twilight” or “the next Harry Potter” but truly it’s a mix of both, and deserves to have a name of</span>
  <span id="freeText10035457144179824206" style="display:none">So I realize I sorta missed the boat with this series as I believe the first one came out in like, 2009. But whatever. I am not really going to talk much about the plot, mostly because throughout 4 books of at least 500 pages each, THERE IS SO MUCH OF IT. However there might be Spoilers, But I’ll make sure and say so before.<br /><br />I think the thing about these books is that they were pitted to be “the next twilight” or “the next Harry Potter” but truly it’s a mix of both, and deserves to have a name of it’s own.<br /><br />While The Caster Chronicles do have that “forbidden love” touch in the first book, and goes on to have quite a few romantic scenes (NOPE. LET’S KEEP IT PG PEOPLE, NOTHING MORE THAN KISSING GET YOUR MIND OUT OF THE GUTTER.) I feel like it goes so much beyond that.<br /><br />Now correct me if I am wrong, (since i’ve never actually read twilight) but I believe it is ALL about Bella and Edwards relationship, and stuff right?<br /><br />Now The Caster Chronicles have that, they have a lot of focus on Ethan and Lena’s relationship, but there is so much more going on in the books.<br /><br />OKAY SPOILER TIME DON’T READ UNLESS YOU’VE FINISHED ALL OF THEM.<br /><br /><br />Ethan and Lena are testing their relationship as Lena goes through several obstacles to face her “claiming” and results in “breaking the order” So now, Ethan and Lena and their friends are in a race against time to fix the order, decide whether Lena is Light or Dark, not get killed AND try to be normal teenagers. <br /><br />And Lena and Ethan aren’t perfect. They make mistakes. And that’s what I love about them, they are so real, and beautifully portrayed. But that’s not all. The Caster Chronicles go beyond a superficial, paranormal romance story.<br /><br />In the 3rd book, Ethan dies in order to saves the ones he loves (TRUST ME, I BAWLED) Ethan is so in love with Lena that he will do anything for her. I mean who doesn’t want to read about a hot, smart, loving, caring guy who dies for his girlfriend to survive? Who believes in her, who travels through these dangerous and terrifying adventures just to get back to her?<br /><br />I just believe that The Caster Chronicles are so much more than “The next twilight”. I want them to be remembered. <br /><br />Because Lena isn’t cool. She isn’t perfect. She doesn’t fit in. She doesn’t know who she is. But she learns. And she is powerful, and she gives everything her all. And if that’s not a role-model, than I don’t know what is.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10035457144179824206" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

I appreciated the various struggles that the characters went through - and that there was depth and complexity to the characters and many of the situations they faced.   <span id="freeText3250169146604732679" style="display:none">I really enjoyed this series. It is a YA/paranormal romance series, like so many that are popular these days. But, it isn't a "canned" series by any means. I appreciated the various struggles that the characters went through - and that there was depth and complexity to the characters and many of the situations they faced. For example, the relationship between Lena and Sarafine is ANYTHING but simple. You want to think it's black and white - that Sarafine is just evil and that's all there is to it, but that's not the case. I was a little disappointed in the final book - "Beautiful Redemption". It was a good read, but I thought it fell a little flat. The whole time I was reading I knew how it would end (basically) and perhaps because of that, the challenges along the way seemed to be too easily overcome. But, we all love a happy ending and we definitely got that.</span>

<div id="review_2581725893" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2581725893" />
    <a title="Ethan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4839193-ethan"><img alt="Ethan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1295482996p2/4839193.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2581725893?book_show_action=true">Nov 08, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ethan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ethan" href="/user/show/4839193-ethan">Ethan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer2581725893&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2581725893" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7744456241425728845"> 	** spoiler alert ** This is generally ok as light reading--it grabs you and it's hard to put down. I have three pretty big problems with the book, though. Firstly, it bums me out to read books where a vast majority of the characters are bad people, especially when they take it much further than I've experienced in reality. I find it really difficult to believe that a whole town would gang up against someone when there is seriously zero evidence against him or her. The major vendetta of all of </span>
  <span id="freeText7744456241425728845" style="display:none"> 	** spoiler alert ** This is generally ok as light reading--it grabs you and it's hard to put down. I have three pretty big problems with the book, though. Firstly, it bums me out to read books where a vast majority of the characters are bad people, especially when they take it much further than I've experienced in reality. I find it really difficult to believe that a whole town would gang up against someone when there is seriously zero evidence against him or her. The major vendetta of all of the students and parents against the Ravenwoods and Duchannes is extreme and worrisome. Additionally, their association with real-world organizations (the DAR, for example) is a little bit rude toward those organizations. I'm sure there are many DAR chapters that would never dream of ostracizing and criminalizing a family in their community the way these characters do. <br />Secondly, a lot of it is derivative of Carrie, Harry Potter, and some other fantasy staples. Maybe it's an homage... but I don't think so. <br />Thirdly (and this is the most important one--I would have given it an easy 4 stars if it weren't for this) I didn't find the plot or the invented concepts to be properly hashed out. There was a lot of correlation without explanation, which is to say that events happen because of each other, but I can't fathom why there's a relation between cause and effect... it's just taken for granted that they're connected. Now, I expect some of you are rolling your eyes (yes, I flatter myself into believing that somebody might read this) and dismissing this as bupkis because it's young adult literature and because it's fantasy, both of which are genres light on explanation. I get that and I actually tend to distinguish fantasy from other genres largely based on whether their actions are explained by science or belief in a higher power. Still, I found that this book was more troubling than most fantasy or young adult literature. <br />In Percy Jackson, they are descendants of gods, hence powers.<br />In Twilight, shapeshifters are hereditary (with a complex backstory of how the powers originated and why they manifest) and vampires are contagious (also with a complex history and with all of the plot point motivated by the personalities and objectives of different characters).<br />Harry Potter actually has similar problems of the magic being whatever the author wants, when she wants it... but at least the spells are consistent and repeatable and the plot is based largely on school years and horcruxes.<br />Then there are world building novels like Dune, Lord of the Rings, Kingkiller, Earthsea, etc, all of which set a precedent in the fantasy world of very well-thought-out concepts of magic with clearly explained parameters, uses, and relationships.<br />In the Caster Chronicles, however, the nature of magic feels like it is written from a very deus ex machina sort of perspective. Each volume hinges on a sacrifice which happens to propel the series forward in a convenient way. They repeatedly declare that spells have costs and consequences, but how come that only applies to the Caster Chronicles (the book within the book, not the series itself) and the Book of Moons? Why does the Book of Moons spell require a human sacrifice if weather magic is free? It seemed inconsistent to me for the archlight to overpower the Book of Moons. How are the consequences of Genevieve's spell established? Who wrote the rules? Is the book of moons actually a side effect of Angelus having rewritten Ethan Carter Wate's page??? If so, just say it. Why would half of the immortals die after the second natural makes her choice? It seems so arbitrary! Why is there a connection between astrology and powers? Why is the water tower a nexus of power? Why and how are we supposed to believe that jumping from there would result in the world being reset??? Nobody has ever reset the world by jumping from a water tower before, so what relationship is there between the water tower jumping and this world reset? I just don't follow this logic. Why do they have to have Ms. English to channel a demon? Why not someone else? Why does the boatman like Ethan and choose to help him? Why is Sarafine Ethan's challenge in the gateway? Why were the keepers established? Why are lillith/demons different from casters if they can all be the offspring of the same people? Why is the only effect of the reset that Lena and Ethan can now kiss without a spark? What is the relationship between the Book of Stars and the Book of Moons? Why must immortals choose light or dark? Why are they called immortals when they can be killed? How did John Breed get in the archlight? How and why do archlights work? Where do archlights come from and why are there so few of them? Why does an archlight work on John Breed when he's not an incubus and he isn't affected by light? How does Ridley make the Holy Rollers' music good? Of all immortal powers to write on your own page of the Caster Chronicles, why did Angelus choose to give himself the power to give people animal body parts? Who was Ethan actually supposed to guide? I thought his powers as a wayward were kept very vague and hence impossible to really evaluate, criticize, or understand.<br /><br />Don't even get me started on the time paradoxes in the last book. Granted, a lot of what I'm about to say is based on my assumption that when he is reborn on the water tower and sees Ama fall, it's taken him back to the moment he would have jumped... but maybe it's not. If not, I don't understand why the direct result of changing the Caster Chronicle is to revive him, but keep everything else the same. I get that the Caster Chronicles are omnipresent through time, but then why isn't it born whole? Why does tearing a page out kill Angelus, but just reset Ethan? How is he reset if his attempt to reset the book is only due to the page being in there? When they reset, are Abraham and Hunting still alive? Why does Xavier say that he'll see him when he dies--wouldn't Ethan have to get another river's eye to pay the boatman in order to visit Xavier? <br /><br /><br />What's more, nothing that happened in most of each book had any impact on the endings. The characters struggle to research, keep secrets, investigate, etc, but what they end up doing has nothing to do with their research and very few of the previous conflicts cause them to grow in a way that helps them overcome the final conflicts. A ton of the characters and events are confusingly complicated and then completely irrelevant. For example, Ethan's dad is totally bizarre, but that never really matters, it's just distracting. Hmmm. Oh well. Major spoiler: Sarafine, Hunter, and Abraham ALL DIE suddenly and with surprising ease even though they are described as being nearly invincible. They die without having accomplished anything and without having even revealed their actual intentions. They die and then, basically, everyone shrugs and moves on. Even Angelus dies in an idiotic and unlikely way, having achieved nothing and never really having revealed his motivations. Sure, he hates mortals, but why does he hate mortals? Why did he hate being a mortal himself? Could we have his backstory from when he started hating mortals, please? I tend to be very critical of children's books, but I think someone ought to be. Just because kids aren't critical, that doesn't justify giving them poorly thought-out stories. <br /><br />Last and least, why were there no jokes about The Music Man made toward Marian, the librarian?</span>
  <a data-text-id="7744456241425728845" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_601301235" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/601301235" />
    <a title="Bethany" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9316985-bethany"><img alt="Bethany" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1344999851p2/9316985.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/601301235?book_show_action=true">Apr 27, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bethany" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bethany" href="/user/show/9316985-bethany">Bethany</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer601301235" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11349617839663926749">Beautiful Creatures—book one				Read: March 2013<br/>By: Kami Garcia & Margaret Stohl<br/>2009 563 pages <br/><br/>It may be present day in Gatlin County, South Carolina, but the town is tied to the past like two apron strings pulling hard to the back, one string to mortals and the other to castors (witches). Ethan Wate is bored with the smallness of the town and the dullness of the citizens, so the new girl in school takes his breath away. Lena Duchannes will be turning 16 and at that time she will be claimed by e</span>
  <span id="freeText11349617839663926749" style="display:none">Beautiful Creatures—book one				Read: March 2013<br />By: Kami Garcia &amp; Margaret Stohl<br />2009 563 pages <br /><br />It may be present day in Gatlin County, South Carolina, but the town is tied to the past like two apron strings pulling hard to the back, one string to mortals and the other to castors (witches). Ethan Wate is bored with the smallness of the town and the dullness of the citizens, so the new girl in school takes his breath away. Lena Duchannes will be turning 16 and at that time she will be claimed by either the dark or the light magic and her eyes will reveal the color of her soul and the intent of her heart. It is a family curse and unknown to two star-crossed lovers, their family trees have intertwined before, around the time that Atlanta was burning.<br />Ethan’s mother has recently died and his father is acting crazy, but fortunately, Amma who raised Ethan’s father and is a seer(voodoo) is determined to keep Ethan from harm, even if that harm is the love of his life. Kelting is introduced as a way for two teens (with super powers) to talk to each other all night, without cell phones. Lena is being raised by her Uncle Macon, who is an incubus (a good one, who feeds on the dreams of people instead of blood). It seems that every member of Lena’s family has a different power.<br />Characters in the town are still waving the Rebel flag and think too much about the social rights and wrongs, while the Castor world buzzes underground, but by the end of this first book, the two worlds are pushed together in a grand birthday party where one dies so that another can live.<br />A locket found at “Greenbrier” gives Lena and Ethan visions of the evil that caused the curse for the Duchanne women, when Ethan’s ancestor fell in love with Lena’s ancestor. Marion, librarian for the town and keeper (light &amp; dark castor/incubus librarian) Ethan’s mother’s best friend, helps Ethan discover what he needs to know.<br /><br /> “Darkness cannot drive out darkness only light can do that. Hate cannot drive out hate; only love can do that.” Martin Luther King Jr.<br /><br />Beautiful Darkness—book two				Read: March 2013<br />By: Kami Garcia &amp; Margaret Stohl<br />2010 503 pages <br /><br />	Love is still there for Ethan and Lena, but it is hidden by sadness, shame, and anger. Lena made a choice, but didn’t realize the price, so she is missing her Uncle Macon. She sees herself turning dark and unable to stop the curse from the Civil War, even though she pulled off a big one by covering the moon so that her 16th moon, was not a claiming. When she looks at Ethan, she is reminded of giving up her uncle and fears the pain she will cause Ethan if she loves him.<br />Ethan’s best friend, Link, falls for Lena’s cousin, Ridley (a siren). Olivia comes on the scene from England to work with Marion, and what a surprise, she too is a keeper, causing Lena lots of jealousy, but then Lena is spending way too much time with the mysterious John Breed, as she tries to drive Ethan safely away from her. Seventeen moons is approaching and this time it seems that Lena will need to choose between light and dark.<br />The tunnels come into play much more in this book, as travel routes for Ethan, Link, and Olivia as they try to find Lena who has run off with John Breed. They travel to a magic island, after stopping in Savannah and meeting Amma in the graveyard with the “Greats” (Amma’s dead Anncestors). Ethan is able to meet with his mother (dead) and learns about the secret romance that Macon and his mother, Lila had before she married his father. Time and space and magic happen in the tunnels and after freeing Uncle Macon from death (he turned into a good castor/now not an incubus) while trapped for safe-keeping in the magic globe. Thanks to one of Ethan’s unusual centurion aunts (Prudence, Mercy, and Grace) they are able to find their way through the tunnels to the meeting place of evil where Abraham (Macon’s grandfather) and Hunting (Macon’s evil incubus brother) plan to change the world to incubus evil with no mortals and no castors. Olivia’s decision to help Ethan will cost Marion, because keepers are not allowed to take sides. Lena is pulled from the altar just in time, but chooses to go both light and dark (one eye green and one eye gold). John Breed disappears, but not before biting Link and turning him into Linkabus (he now has power) and Ridley loses all her magic, because she helped Ethan. It seems to be that although everyone pulled away from the evil trap, they have turned the worlds upside down and changed the order of things. There’s going to be a price.<br />Marian, “We don’t get to choose what is true. We only get to choose what we do about it.” [Amma does crosswords and Marian does quotes] (The authors are English teachers!)<br />Beautiful Chaos—book three			Read: April 2013<br />By: Kami Garcia &amp; Margaret Stohl<br />2011 516 pages <br />Lena has one green eye and one gold eye, which reveals that she has chosen to be both light and dark and that has changed the “order of the universe”. . . The world, especially Gatlin. Ethan’s best friend, Link, is no longer just Link, but has turned into “Linkubus” and Ridley, poor thing, had all of her magic stripped from her, but of course she figured out a way around that. It will be the 18th moon by the end of this book, but what does that mean anyway . . . one of the puzzles to be solved, because it doesn’t represent anyone’s birthday.<br />Gatlin begins to suffer through locust, extreme heat, and tornadoes, along with many other natural happenings. The religious in town think it is the second coming, but those in the Castor, Seer, and Inkubus world know that the order is shifting and “The Far Keep” that sets in judgment of that magical world is deciding how exactly all of this will be settled, someone has to pay for the breaking of the rules. One ripping storm tore through town and destroyed the aunts home, placing Prudence in a coma and forcing the other two aunts to live at Ethan’s home. Ridley becomes the cheerleaders best friend and Link is the hunk every girl wants. Olivia by the end of the book falls in love with the most unusual creature and Ethan finds a secret passage way from his house through the tunnels to not only “The Far Keep” but also the future. The end feels like it must be the “real end” when one of the main characters gives the life that the order seems to need to correct itself, but no one is happy and book four, Beautiful Redemption cannot come soon enough.<br />Tumult and peace, the darkness and the light---<br />"Were all like workings of one mind, the features<br />Of the same face, blossoms upon one tree;<br />Characters of the great Apocalypse,<br />The types and symbols of Eternity.<br />Of first, and last, and midst, and without end."<br />William Wordsworth, The Prelude: Book Sixth<br />Beautiful Redemption—book four				Read: April 2013<br />By: Kami Garcia &amp; Margaret Stohl<br />2012 451 pages <br /><br />The last book is divided into three sections, with Ethan being the title of two of those sections and Lena the title of the middle section. It is up to Ethan to figure out if the impossible can be achieved, (the past changed, the book rewritten). After all, it was all a mistake, or rather a contrived mistake by one really greedy guy who is one of the tribunal at “The Far Keep” Ethan is on his own journey to right the wrong and thankfully Amma made him appreciate the crossword puzzle. It takes friends and faith and lots of blocks falling into place for the world to be made whole again. <br />The places that Ethan goes and the actions he must perform are so well described that I felt I needed to take a shower to get rid of the stench of evil. Yena stayed true to the memory of Ethan and never let her dream of his return waiver. <br />There is a certain amount of comfort in seeing where the soul can be worked on and the life of someone be saved. Real or not . . . it is a journey never to be forgotten and Ethan’s courage in the face of unbelievable odds warms the heart of the reader. There is nothing that makes a person appreciate life more than having it taken away.<br />A Seer’s moons, a Siren’s tears,<br />Nineteen Mortal, Wayward Fears,<br />Incubus graves and Caster rivers,<br />The Final Page the End delivers.<br />Kami Garcia and Margaret Stohl delivered a sweeping Four-Book tale that transports the reader to a world of magic and romance, in a world so close, but yet unreachable. I enjoyed reading about the characters and appreciated Amma’s crossword puzzle words and Marian’s reference to good literature throughout all four books. Mary and I went to see the movie, but they ruined it in Hollywood and tried to squeeze out an apple to represent a whole fruit market, what a shame.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11349617839663926749" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('PeRDGQH27Y1qzlTwfAYsma7as3os5u3RRTcUVEqT51eJSSf9SMGBkpQJ0gdKNFNS8Ekyw81B/qcjHsxsLMNgSA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('phkjyKaYpQS+izyG5J257exao5dyX0mEkC4M2wBMfCAStEcs76/JG0BMunHSr8YmsskiLpP4WvL2B9TjZhz7Pw==')})
  }

How could a mere human survive such an attack. \nIn the second novel, City of Ashes, Clary just wants her life to go back to normal--but that turns out to be impossible. For one thing, her mother is still in the hospital, in a mysterious coma. For another, she and her newfound brother Jace have fallen under a cloud of suspicion now that the Shadowhunter world knows that Valentine is still alive--and that Jace and Clary are his son and daughter. Then Clary\'s best friend Simon is turned into a vampire and kidnapped by Valentine, who intends to sacrifice him as part of a bloody ritual that will make the Mortal Instruments Valentine\'s forever. \n\nIn book three, City of Glass, Clary has to use all her ingenuity and newfound magical skills to get herself to the Glass City in Idris, the secretive Shadowhunters\' home country, where she is forbidden to go--for it is only there that she can find the cure to the enchanted sleeping sickness to which her mother has succumbed. When Valentine attacks the city and destroys the demon towers, Clary and her allies are all that stand between him and the total annihilation of all Shadowhunters. <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer4667360342685577395">Kami Garcia is a #1 New York Times, USA Today, and international bestselling author. She is the coauthor of the BEAUTIFUL CREATURES series, which has been published in 51 countries and 37 languages, with over 10 million copies in print. In 2013, Beautiful Creatures released as a feature film from Warner Brothers. Kami is a cofounder of the YALLFEST kid lit book festival and the author of five solo</span>
  <span id="freeText4667360342685577395" style="display:none">Kami Garcia is a #1 New York Times, USA Today, and international bestselling author. She is the coauthor of the BEAUTIFUL CREATURES series, which has been published in 51 countries and 37 languages, with over 10 million copies in print. In 2013, Beautiful Creatures released as a feature film from Warner Brothers. Kami is a cofounder of the YALLFEST kid lit book festival and the author of five solo novels, including her Bram Stoker Award-nominated novels Unbreakable and Unmarked (THE LEGION series) and The X-Files Origins: Agent of Chaos. Kami’s first graphic novel Teen Titans: Raven, with artist Gabriel Picolo, is the first book in her TEEN TITANS series for DC Comics and the adult series JOKER/HARLEY: CRIMINAL SANITY, from DC Black Label.<br /><br />Find Kami online at kamigarcia.com, on Facebook @KamiGarciaYA, and on Twitter and Instagram @KamiGarcia. </span>
